<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Dentistry</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="contentSub2"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>

<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>

</p>

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dental_surgery_aboard_USS_Eisenhower,_January_1990.JPEG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2810" data-file-width="1880" decoding="async" height="329" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Dental_surgery_aboard_USS_Eisenhower%2C_January_1990.JPEG/220px-Dental_surgery_aboard_USS_Eisenhower%2C_January_1990.JPEG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Dental_surgery_aboard_USS_Eisenhower%2C_January_1990.JPEG/330px-Dental_surgery_aboard_USS_Eisenhower%2C_January_1990.JPEG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Dental_surgery_aboard_USS_Eisenhower%2C_January_1990.JPEG/440px-Dental_surgery_aboard_USS_Eisenhower%2C_January_1990.JPEG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dental_surgery_aboard_USS_Eisenhower,_January_1990.JPEG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oral_surgeon" title="Oral surgeon">oral surgeon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dental_assistant" title="Dental assistant">dental assistant</a> removing a <a href="/wiki/Wisdom_tooth" title="Wisdom tooth">wisdom tooth</a></div></div></div>
<p><b>Dentistry</b>, also known as <b>dental medicine</b> and <b><a href="/wiki/Oral_medicine" title="Oral medicine">oral medicine</a></b>, is the branch of <a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">medicine</a> focused on the <a href="/wiki/Human_tooth" title="Human tooth">teeth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gums" title="Gums">gums</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Human_mouth" title="Human mouth">mouth</a>. It consists of the study, <a href="/wiki/Diagnosis" title="Diagnosis">diagnosis</a>, prevention, management, and treatment of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diseases" title="Diseases">diseases</a>, disorders, and conditions of the mouth, most commonly focused on <a href="/wiki/Dentition" title="Dentition">dentition</a> (the development and arrangement of teeth) as well as the <a href="/wiki/Oral_mucosa" title="Oral mucosa">oral mucosa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[2]</a></sup> Dentistry may also encompass other aspects of the <a href="/wiki/Craniofacial" title="Craniofacial">craniofacial</a> complex including the <a href="/wiki/Temporomandibular_joint" title="Temporomandibular joint">temporomandibular joint</a>. The practitioner is called a <a href="/wiki/Dentist" title="Dentist">dentist</a>.
</p><p>The history of dentistry is almost as ancient as the history of humanity and civilization with the earliest evidence dating from 7000 BC to 5500 BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-4">[3]</a></sup> Dentistry is thought to have been the first specialization in <a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">medicine</a> which have gone on to develop its own accredited degree with its own specializations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Suddick1990_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Suddick1990-5">[4]</a></sup> Dentistry is often also understood to subsume the now largely defunct <a href="/wiki/Medical_specialty" title="Medical specialty">medical specialty</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stomatology" title="Stomatology">stomatology</a> (the study of the mouth and its disorders and diseases) for which reason the two terms are used interchangeably in certain regions. However, some specialties such as <a href="/wiki/Oral_and_maxillofacial_surgery" title="Oral and maxillofacial surgery">oral and maxillofacial surgery</a> (facial reconstruction) may require both medical and dental degrees to accomplish. In European history, dentistry is considered to have stemmed from the trade of <a href="/wiki/Barber_surgeon" title="Barber surgeon">barber surgeons</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[5]</a></sup>
</p><p>Dental treatments are carried out by a dental team, which often consists of a <a href="/wiki/Dentist" title="Dentist">dentist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dental_auxiliary" title="Dental auxiliary">dental auxiliaries</a> (<a href="/wiki/Dental_assistant" title="Dental assistant">dental assistants</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dental_hygienist" title="Dental hygienist">dental hygienists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dental_technician" title="Dental technician">dental technicians</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Dental_therapist" title="Dental therapist">dental therapists</a>). Most dentists either work in private practices (<a href="/wiki/Primary_care" title="Primary care">primary care</a>), dental hospitals or (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secondary_care" title="Secondary care">secondary care</a>) institutions (prisons, armed forces bases, etc.).
</p><p>The modern movement of <a href="/wiki/Evidence-based_dentistry" title="Evidence-based dentistry">evidence-based dentistry</a> calls for the use of high-quality scientific research and evidence to guide decision-making such as in manual tooth conservation, use of fluoride water treatment and fluoride toothpaste, dealing with oral diseases such as <a href="/wiki/Tooth_decay" title="Tooth decay">tooth decay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Periodontal_disease" title="Periodontal disease">periodontitis</a>, as well as systematic diseases such as <a href="/wiki/Osteoporosis" title="Osteoporosis">osteoporosis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diabetes" title="Diabetes">diabetes</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Celiac_disease" title="Celiac disease">celiac disease</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cancer" title="Cancer">cancer</a>, <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a> which could also affect the oral cavity. Other practices relevant to <a href="/wiki/Evidence-based_dentistry" title="Evidence-based dentistry">evidence-based dentistry</a> include <a href="/wiki/Radiology" title="Radiology">radiology</a> of the mouth to inspect teeth deformity or oral malaises, <a href="/wiki/Hematology" title="Hematology">haematology</a> (study of blood) to avoid bleeding complications during dental surgery, <a href="/wiki/Cardiology" title="Cardiology">cardiology</a> (due to various severe complications arising from dental surgery with patients with heart disease), etc.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminology">Terminology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dentistry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Terminology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The term dentistry comes from <i>dentist</i>, which comes from French <i>dentiste</i>, which comes from the French and Latin words for tooth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[6]</a></sup> The term for the associated scientific study of teeth is <b>odontology</b> (from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek_language" title="Ancient Greek language">Ancient Greek</a>: <span lang="grc">ὀδούς</span>, <small><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Ancient_Greek" title="Romanization of Ancient Greek">romanized</a>: </small><span title="Ancient Greek-language romanization"><i lang="grc-Latn">odoús</i></span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Literal_translation" title="Literal translation">lit.</a> </small>'tooth') – the study of the structure, development, and abnormalities of the teeth.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Dental_treatment">Dental treatment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dentistry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Dental treatment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Dentistry usually encompasses practices related to the oral cavity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gambhir2015_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gambhir2015-8">[7]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a>, oral diseases are major public health problems due to their high incidence and prevalence across the globe, with the disadvantaged affected more than other socio-economic groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHOoraldisease_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-WHOoraldisease-9">[8]</a></sup>
</p><p>The majority of dental treatments are carried out to prevent or treat the two most common <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dental_disease" title="Dental disease">oral diseases</a> which are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dental_caries" title="Dental caries">dental caries</a> (tooth decay) and <a href="/wiki/Periodontal_disease" title="Periodontal disease">periodontal disease</a> (gum disease or pyorrhea). Common treatments involve the <a href="/wiki/Dental_restoration" title="Dental restoration">restoration of teeth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dental_extraction" title="Dental extraction">extraction</a> or surgical removal of teeth, <a href="/wiki/Scaling_and_root_planing" title="Scaling and root planing">scaling and root planing</a>, endodontic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endodontic_therapy" title="Endodontic therapy">root canal</a> treatment, and <a href="/wiki/Cosmetic_dentistry" title="Cosmetic dentistry">cosmetic dentistry</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[9]</a></sup>
</p><p>By nature of their general training, dentists, without specialization can carry out the majority of dental treatments such as restorative (fillings, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crown_(dentistry)" title="Crown (dentistry)">crowns</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bridge_(dentistry)" title="Bridge (dentistry)">bridges</a>), prosthetic (<a href="/wiki/Dentures" title="Dentures">dentures</a>), endodontic (root canal) therapy, periodontal (gum) therapy, and extraction of teeth, as well as performing examinations, radiographs (x-rays), and diagnosis. Dentists can also prescribe medications such as <a href="/wiki/Antibiotic" title="Antibiotic">antibiotics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sedative" title="Sedative">sedatives</a>, and any other drugs used in patient management. Depending on their licensing boards, general dentists may be required to complete additional training to perform sedation, dental implants, etc.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Enamel_celiac.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="746" data-file-width="1161" decoding="async" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Enamel_celiac.jpg/220px-Enamel_celiac.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Enamel_celiac.jpg/330px-Enamel_celiac.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Enamel_celiac.jpg/440px-Enamel_celiac.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Enamel_celiac.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Irreversible enamel defects caused by an untreated celiac disease. They may be the only clue to its diagnosis, even in absence of gastrointestinal symptoms, but are often confused with fluorosis, <a href="/wiki/Tetracycline" title="Tetracycline">tetracycline</a> discoloration, acid reflux or other causes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIHCDdiagnosis_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-NIHCDdiagnosis-11">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIHCDdentalenamel_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-NIHCDdentalenamel-12">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PastoreCarroccio2008_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-PastoreCarroccio2008-13">[12]</a></sup> The National Institutes of Health include a dental exam in the diagnostic protocol of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Celiac_disease" title="Celiac disease">celiac disease</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIHCDdiagnosis_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-NIHCDdiagnosis-11">[10]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Dentists also encourage prevention of oral diseases through proper <a href="/wiki/Hygiene" title="Hygiene">hygiene</a> and regular, twice or more yearly, checkups for professional cleaning and evaluation. Oral infections and inflammations may affect overall health and conditions in the oral cavity may be indicative of systemic diseases, such as <a href="/wiki/Osteoporosis" title="Osteoporosis">osteoporosis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diabetes" title="Diabetes">diabetes</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Celiac_disease" title="Celiac disease">celiac disease</a> or <a href="/wiki/Cancer" title="Cancer">cancer</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gambhir2015_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gambhir2015-8">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIHCDdiagnosis_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-NIHCDdiagnosis-11">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EstrellaBoynton2010_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-EstrellaBoynton2010-14">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-daFonseca2010_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-daFonseca2010-15">[14]</a></sup> Many studies have also shown that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gum_disease" title="Gum disease">gum disease</a> is associated with an increased risk of diabetes, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heart_disease" title="Heart disease">heart disease</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Preterm_birth" title="Preterm birth">preterm birth</a>. The concept that oral health can affect systemic health and disease is referred to as "oral-systemic health".
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education_and_licensing">Education and licensing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dentistry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Education and licensing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dentistry_throughout_the_world" title="Dentistry throughout the world">Dentistry throughout the world</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cross_sections_of_teeth_labels.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3453" data-file-width="3453" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Cross_sections_of_teeth_labels.png/220px-Cross_sections_of_teeth_labels.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Cross_sections_of_teeth_labels.png/330px-Cross_sections_of_teeth_labels.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Cross_sections_of_teeth_labels.png/440px-Cross_sections_of_teeth_labels.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cross_sections_of_teeth_labels.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A sagittal cross-section of a molar tooth; 1: crown, 2: root, 3: enamel, 4: dentin and dentin tubules, 5: pulp chamber, 6: blood vessels and nerve, 7: periodontal ligament, 8: apex and periapical region, 9: alveolar bone</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Early_dental_chair,_Shamrock,_TX_IMG_6151.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Early_dental_chair%2C_Shamrock%2C_TX_IMG_6151.JPG/220px-Early_dental_chair%2C_Shamrock%2C_TX_IMG_6151.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Early_dental_chair%2C_Shamrock%2C_TX_IMG_6151.JPG/330px-Early_dental_chair%2C_Shamrock%2C_TX_IMG_6151.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Early_dental_chair%2C_Shamrock%2C_TX_IMG_6151.JPG/440px-Early_dental_chair%2C_Shamrock%2C_TX_IMG_6151.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Early_dental_chair,_Shamrock,_TX_IMG_6151.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Early dental chair in <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Pioneer_West_Museum&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Pioneer West Museum (page does not exist)">Pioneer West Museum</a> in <a href="/wiki/Shamrock,_Texas" title="Shamrock, Texas">Shamrock, Texas</a></div></div></div>
<p>John M. Harris started the world's first dental school in <a href="/wiki/Bainbridge,_Ross_County,_Ohio" title="Bainbridge, Ross County, Ohio">Bainbridge, Ohio</a>, and helped to establish dentistry as a health profession. It opened on 21 February 1828, and today is a <a href="/wiki/Harris_Dental_Museum" title="Harris Dental Museum">dental museum</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup> The first dental college, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore_College_of_Dental_Surgery" title="Baltimore College of Dental Surgery">Baltimore College of Dental Surgery</a>, opened in Baltimore, Maryland, US in 1840. The second in the United States was the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_College_of_Dental_Surgery" title="Ohio College of Dental Surgery">Ohio College of Dental Surgery</a>, established in Cincinnati, Ohio, in 1845.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania_School_of_Dental_Medicine" title="University of Pennsylvania School of Dental Medicine">Philadelphia College of Dental Surgery</a> followed in 1852.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[17]</a></sup> In 1907, <a href="/wiki/Temple_University" title="Temple University">Temple University</a> accepted a bid to incorporate the school.
</p><p>Studies show that dentists that graduated from different countries,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup> or even from different dental schools in one country,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup> may make different clinical decisions for the same clinical condition. For example, dentists that graduated from <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israeli</a> dental schools may recommend the removal of asymptomatic <a href="/wiki/Tooth_impaction" title="Tooth impaction">impacted</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Third_molar" title="Third molar">third molar</a> (wisdom teeth) more often than dentists that graduated from Latin American or Eastern European dental schools.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the United Kingdom, the first dental schools, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/London_School_of_Dental_Surgery" title="London School of Dental Surgery">London School of Dental Surgery</a> and the Metropolitan School of Dental Science, both in London, opened in 1859.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MedHist2005_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-MedHist2005-22">[21]</a></sup> The British Dentists Act of 1878 and the 1879 Dentists Register limited the title of "dentist" and "dental surgeon" to qualified and registered practitioners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125years_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-125years-23">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bdatimeline_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-bdatimeline-24">[23]</a></sup> However, others could legally describe themselves as "dental experts" or "dental consultants".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup> The practice of dentistry in the United Kingdom became fully regulated with the 1921 Dentists Act, which required the registration of anyone practising dentistry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/British_Dental_Association" title="British Dental Association">British Dental Association</a>, formed in 1880 with Sir <a href="/wiki/John_Tomes" title="John Tomes">John Tomes</a> as president, played a major role in prosecuting dentists practising illegally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125years_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-125years-23">[22]</a></sup> Dentists in the United Kingdom are now regulated by the <a href="/wiki/General_Dental_Council" title="General Dental Council">General Dental Council</a>.
</p><p>In many countries, dentists usually complete between five and eight years of post-secondary education before practising. Though not mandatory, many dentists choose to complete an internship or residency focusing on specific aspects of dental care after they have received their dental degree. In a few countries, to become a qualified dentist one must usually complete at least four years of postgraduate study;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dental_degree" title="Dental degree">Dental degrees</a> awarded around the world include the Doctor of Dental Surgery (DDS) and Doctor of Dental Medicine (DMD) in North America (US and Canada), and the Bachelor of Dental Surgery/Baccalaureus Dentalis Chirurgiae (BDS, BDent, BChD, BDSc) in the UK and current and former British Commonwealth countries. 
</p><p>All dentists in the United States undergo at least three years of undergraduate studies, but nearly all complete a bachelor's degree. This schooling is followed by four years of dental school to qualify as a "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Dental_Surgery" title="Doctor of Dental Surgery">Doctor of Dental Surgery</a>" (DDS) or "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Dental_Medicine" title="Doctor of Dental Medicine">Doctor of Dental Medicine</a>" (DMD). Specialization in dentistry is available in the fields of Anesthesiology, Dental Public Health, Endodontics, Oral Radiology, Oral Maxillofacial Surgery, Oral Medicine, Orofacial Pain, Pathology, Orthodontics, Pediatric Dentistry, Periodontics, and Prosthodontics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Specialties">Specialties <span class="anchor" id="Specialities"></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dentistry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Specialties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Specialty_(dentistry)" title="Specialty (dentistry)">Specialty (dentistry)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Armilan_hammashoitola,_Lappeenranta.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="4608" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Armilan_hammashoitola%2C_Lappeenranta.jpg/220px-Armilan_hammashoitola%2C_Lappeenranta.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Armilan_hammashoitola%2C_Lappeenranta.jpg/330px-Armilan_hammashoitola%2C_Lappeenranta.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Armilan_hammashoitola%2C_Lappeenranta.jpg/440px-Armilan_hammashoitola%2C_Lappeenranta.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Armilan_hammashoitola,_Lappeenranta.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A modern dental clinic in <a href="/wiki/Lappeenranta" title="Lappeenranta">Lappeenranta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a></div></div></div>
<p>Some dentists undertake further training after their initial degree in order to specialize. Exactly which subjects are recognized by dental registration bodies varies according to location. Examples include:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Cosmetic_dentistry" title="Cosmetic dentistry">Cosmetic dentistry</a>- Focuses on improving the appearance of the mouth, teeth and smile.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dental_anesthesiology" title="Dental anesthesiology">Anesthesiology</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup> –  The specialty of dentistry that deals with the advanced use of general anesthesia, sedation and pain management to facilitate dental procedures.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dental_public_health" title="Dental public health">Dental public health</a> – The study of <a href="/wiki/Epidemiology" title="Epidemiology">epidemiology</a> and social health policies relevant to oral health.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Endodontics" title="Endodontics">Endodontics</a> (also called <i>endodontology</i>) – <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Root_canal_therapy" title="Root canal therapy">Root canal therapy</a> and study of diseases of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dental_pulp" title="Dental pulp">dental pulp</a> and periapical tissues.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Forensic_odontology" title="Forensic odontology">Forensic odontology</a> – The gathering and use of dental evidence in law. This may be performed by any <a href="/wiki/Dentist" title="Dentist">dentist</a> with experience or training in this field. The function of the forensic dentist is primarily documentation and verification of identity.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Geriatric_dentistry" title="Geriatric dentistry">Geriatric dentistry</a> or <i>geriodontics</i> – The delivery of dental care to older adults involving the diagnosis, prevention, and treatment of problems associated with normal aging and age-related diseases as part of an interdisciplinary team with other health care professionals.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Oral_and_maxillofacial_pathology" title="Oral and maxillofacial pathology">Oral and maxillofacial pathology</a> – The study, diagnosis, and sometimes the treatment of oral and maxillofacial related diseases.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Oral_and_maxillofacial_radiology" title="Oral and maxillofacial radiology">Oral and maxillofacial radiology</a> – The study and radiologic interpretation of oral and maxillofacial diseases.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Oral_and_maxillofacial_surgery" title="Oral and maxillofacial surgery">Oral and maxillofacial surgery</a> (also called <i>oral surgery</i>) – <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extraction_(dental)" title="Extraction (dental)">Extractions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dental_implant" title="Dental implant">implants</a>, and surgery of the jaws, mouth and face.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[nb 2]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Oral_biology&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Oral biology (page does not exist)">Oral biology</a> – Research in dental and craniofacial biology</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oral_Implantology" title="Oral Implantology">Oral Implantology</a> – The art and science of replacing extracted teeth with dental implants.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Oral_medicine" title="Oral medicine">Oral medicine</a> – The clinical evaluation and <a href="/wiki/Medical_diagnosis" title="Medical diagnosis">diagnosis</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oral_cavity" title="Oral cavity">oral</a> <a href="/wiki/Oral_mucosa" title="Oral mucosa">mucosal</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oral_pathology" title="Oral pathology">diseases</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Orthodontics" title="Orthodontics">Orthodontics</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Dentofacial_orthopedics&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Dentofacial orthopedics (page does not exist)">dentofacial orthopedics</a>  – The straightening of teeth and modification of midface and mandibular growth.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pediatric_dentistry" title="Pediatric dentistry">Pediatric dentistry</a> (also called <i>pedodontics</i>) – Dentistry for children</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Periodontology" title="Periodontology">Periodontology</a> (also called <i>periodontics</i>) – The study and treatment of diseases of the <a href="/wiki/Periodontium" title="Periodontium">periodontium</a> (non-surgical and surgical) as well as placement and maintenance of dental implants</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Prosthodontics" title="Prosthodontics">Prosthodontics</a> (also called <i>prosthetic dentistry</i>) – <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Denture" title="Denture">Dentures</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bridge_(dentistry)" title="Bridge (dentistry)">bridges</a> and the restoration of implants.
<ul><li>Some prosthodontists super-specialize in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maxillofacial_prosthetics" title="Maxillofacial prosthetics">maxillofacial prosthetics</a>, which is the discipline originally concerned with the rehabilitation of patients with congenital facial and oral defects such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cleft_lip_and_palate" title="Cleft lip and palate">cleft lip and palate</a> or patients born with an underdeveloped ear (<a href="/wiki/Microtia" title="Microtia">microtia</a>). Today, most maxillofacial prosthodontists return function and esthetics to patients with acquired defects secondary to surgical removal of head and neck tumors, or secondary to trauma from war or motor vehicle accidents.</li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Special_needs_dentistry" title="Special needs dentistry">Special needs dentistry</a> (also called <i>special care dentistry</i>) – Dentistry for those with developmental and acquired disabilities.</li>
<li>Sports dentistry – the branch of <a href="/wiki/Sports_medicine" title="Sports medicine">sports medicine</a> dealing with prevention and treatment of dental injuries and oral diseases associated with sports and exercise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[29]</a></sup> The sports dentist works as an individual consultant or as a member of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sports_Medicine" title="Sports Medicine">Sports Medicine</a> Team.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Veterinary_dentistry" title="Veterinary dentistry">Veterinary dentistry</a> – The field of dentistry applied to the care of animals.  It is a specialty of <a href="/wiki/Veterinary_medicine" title="Veterinary medicine">veterinary medicine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[31]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dentistry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_dental_treatments" title="History of dental treatments">History of dental treatments</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_wealthy_patient_falling_over_because_of_having_a_tooth_ext_Wellcome_V0012058.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3072" data-file-width="2376" decoding="async" height="284" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/A_wealthy_patient_falling_over_because_of_having_a_tooth_ext_Wellcome_V0012058.jpg/220px-A_wealthy_patient_falling_over_because_of_having_a_tooth_ext_Wellcome_V0012058.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/A_wealthy_patient_falling_over_because_of_having_a_tooth_ext_Wellcome_V0012058.jpg/330px-A_wealthy_patient_falling_over_because_of_having_a_tooth_ext_Wellcome_V0012058.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/A_wealthy_patient_falling_over_because_of_having_a_tooth_ext_Wellcome_V0012058.jpg/440px-A_wealthy_patient_falling_over_because_of_having_a_tooth_ext_Wellcome_V0012058.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_wealthy_patient_falling_over_because_of_having_a_tooth_ext_Wellcome_V0012058.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>"A wealthy patient falling over because of having a tooth extracted with such vigour by a fashionable dentist", c. 1790. History of Dentistry.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Johann_Liss_002a.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2421" data-file-width="1925" decoding="async" height="277" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Johann_Liss_002a.jpg/220px-Johann_Liss_002a.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Johann_Liss_002a.jpg/330px-Johann_Liss_002a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Johann_Liss_002a.jpg/440px-Johann_Liss_002a.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Johann_Liss_002a.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Farmer at the dentist</i>, <a href="/wiki/Johann_Liss" title="Johann Liss">Johann Liss</a>, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1616–17</span></div></div></div>
<p>Tooth decay was low in <a href="/wiki/Paleolithic_diet" title="Paleolithic diet">pre-agricultural</a> societies, but the advent of <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">farming</a> society about 10,000 years ago correlated with an increase in <a href="/wiki/Tooth_decay" title="Tooth decay">tooth decay</a> (cavities).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[32]</a></sup> An infected tooth from Italy partially cleaned with flint tools, between 13,820 and 14,160 years old, represents the oldest known dentistry,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[33]</a></sup> although a 2017 study suggests that 130,000 years ago the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neanderthals" title="Neanderthals">Neanderthals</a> already used rudimentary dentistry tools.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[34]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indus_valley" title="Indus valley">Indus valley</a> has yielded evidence of dentistry being practised as far back as 7000 BC, during the <a href="/wiki/Stone_Age" title="Stone Age">Stone Age</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Coppa_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Coppa-37">[35]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neolithic_India" title="Neolithic India">Neolithic</a> site of <a href="/wiki/Mehrgarh" title="Mehrgarh">Mehrgarh</a> (now in Pakistan's south western province of <a href="/wiki/Balochistan" title="Balochistan">Balochistan</a>) indicates that this form of dentistry involved curing tooth related disorders with <a href="/wiki/Bow_drill" title="Bow drill">bow drills</a> operated, perhaps, by skilled bead-crafters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-4">[3]</a></sup> The reconstruction of this ancient form of dentistry showed that the methods used were reliable and effective.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[36]</a></sup> The earliest <a href="/wiki/Dental_restoration" title="Dental restoration">dental filling</a>, made of <a href="/wiki/Beeswax" title="Beeswax">beeswax</a>, was discovered in <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a> and dates from 6500 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[37]</a></sup> Dentistry was practised in prehistoric <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a>, as evidenced by a skull which had a <a href="/wiki/Dental_abscess" title="Dental abscess">dental abscess</a> lanced from the root of a tooth dating back to around 2500 BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[38]</a></sup>
</p><p>An ancient <a href="/wiki/Sumerian_language" title="Sumerian language">Sumerian</a> text describes a "<a href="/wiki/Tooth_worm" title="Tooth worm">tooth worm</a>" as the cause of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dental_caries" title="Dental caries">dental caries</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-adahistory_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-adahistory-41">[39]</a></sup> Evidence of this belief has also been found in ancient India, <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, Japan, and China. The legend of the worm is also found in the <i><a href="/wiki/Homeric_Hymns" title="Homeric Hymns">Homeric Hymns</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[40]</a></sup> and as late as the 14th century AD the surgeon <a href="/wiki/Guy_de_Chauliac" title="Guy de Chauliac">Guy de Chauliac</a> still promoted the belief that worms cause tooth decay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-suddickhistorical_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-suddickhistorical-43">[41]</a></sup>
</p><p>Recipes for the treatment of toothache, infections and loose teeth are spread throughout the <a href="/wiki/Ebers_Papyrus" title="Ebers Papyrus">Ebers Papyrus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kahun_Papyri" title="Kahun Papyri">Kahun Papyri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brugsch_Papyrus" title="Brugsch Papyrus">Brugsch Papyrus</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hearst_papyrus" title="Hearst papyrus">Hearst papyrus</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">Ancient Egypt</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blomstedt_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-blomstedt-44">[42]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Smith_Papyrus" title="Edwin Smith Papyrus">Edwin Smith Papyrus</a>, written in the 17th century BC but which may reflect previous manuscripts from as early as 3000 BC, discusses the treatment of dislocated or fractured jaws.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blomstedt_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-blomstedt-44">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[43]</a></sup> In the 18th century BC, the <a href="/wiki/Code_of_Hammurabi" title="Code of Hammurabi">Code of Hammurabi</a> referenced dental extraction twice as it related to punishment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[44]</a></sup> Examination of the remains of some <a href="/wiki/History_of_ancient_Egypt" title="History of ancient Egypt">ancient Egyptians</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greco-Roman" title="Greco-Roman">Greco-Romans</a> reveals early attempts at dental <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prosthetic" title="Prosthetic">prosthetics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[45]</a></sup> However, it is possible the prosthetics were prepared after death for aesthetic reasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blomstedt_44-2"><a href="#cite_note-blomstedt-44">[42]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Ancient Greek</a> scholars <a href="/wiki/Hippocrates" title="Hippocrates">Hippocrates</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aristotle" title="Aristotle">Aristotle</a> wrote about dentistry, including the eruption pattern of teeth, treating decayed teeth and gum disease, extracting teeth with <a href="/wiki/Forceps" title="Forceps">forceps</a>, and using wires to stabilize loose teeth and fractured jaws.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-History_Of_Dentistry_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-History_Of_Dentistry-48">[46]</a></sup> Some say the first use of dental appliances or <a href="/wiki/Bridge_(dentistry)" title="Bridge (dentistry)">bridges</a> comes from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Etruscans" title="Etruscans">Etruscans</a> from as early as 700 BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[47]</a></sup> In ancient Egypt, <a href="/wiki/Hesy-Ra" title="Hesy-Ra">Hesy-Ra</a> is the first named "dentist" (greatest of the teeth). The Egyptians bound replacement teeth together with gold wire. <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Roman</a> medical writer <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cornelius_Celsus" title="Cornelius Celsus">Cornelius Celsus</a> wrote extensively of oral diseases as well as dental treatments such as narcotic-containing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emollients" title="Emollients">emollients</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Astringents" title="Astringents">astringents</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[48]</a></sup> The earliest <a href="/wiki/Amalgam_(dentistry)" title="Amalgam (dentistry)">dental amalgams</a> were first documented in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tang_Dynasty" title="Tang Dynasty">Tang Dynasty</a> medical text written by the Chinese physician Su Kung in 659, and appeared in Germany in 1528.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bjørklund1_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bjørklund1-51">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-czarnetzki_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-czarnetzki-52">[50]</a></sup>
</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age" title="Islamic Golden Age">Islamic Golden Age</a> Dentistry was discussed in several famous books of medicine such as <a href="/wiki/The_Canon_of_Medicine" title="The Canon of Medicine">The Canon in medicine</a> written by <a href="/wiki/Avicenna" title="Avicenna">Avicenna</a> and Al-Tasreef by <a href="/wiki/Al-Zahrawi" title="Al-Zahrawi">Al-Zahrawi</a> who is considered the greatest <a href="/wiki/Surgeon" title="Surgeon">surgeon</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Middle_ages" title="Middle ages">Middle ages</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[51]</a></sup> Avicenna said that jaw fracture should be reduced according to the occlusal guidance of the teeth; this principle is still valid in modern times. Al-Zahrawi invented over 200 surgical tools that resemble the modern kind.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[52]</a></sup>
</p><p>Historically, dental extractions have been used to treat a variety of illnesses. During the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> and throughout the 19th century, dentistry was not a profession in itself, and often dental procedures were performed by barbers or general <a href="/wiki/Physician" title="Physician">physicians</a>. <a href="/wiki/Barber" title="Barber">Barbers</a> usually limited their practice to extracting teeth which alleviated <a href="/wiki/Pain" title="Pain">pain</a> and associated chronic tooth <a href="/wiki/Infection" title="Infection">infection</a>. Instruments used for dental extractions date back several centuries. In the 14th century, <a href="/wiki/Guy_de_Chauliac" title="Guy de Chauliac">Guy de Chauliac</a> most probably invented the dental pelican<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[53]</a></sup> (resembling a <a href="/wiki/Pelican" title="Pelican">pelican</a>'s beak) which was used to perform <a href="/wiki/Dental_extraction" title="Dental extraction">dental extractions</a> up until the late 18th century. The pelican was replaced by the <a href="/wiki/Dental_key" title="Dental key">dental key</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[54]</a></sup> which, in turn, was replaced by modern forceps in the 19th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[55]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Device-teeth-fauchard.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="820" data-file-width="532" decoding="async" height="339" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Device-teeth-fauchard.jpg/220px-Device-teeth-fauchard.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Device-teeth-fauchard.jpg/330px-Device-teeth-fauchard.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Device-teeth-fauchard.jpg/440px-Device-teeth-fauchard.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Device-teeth-fauchard.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Dental <a href="/wiki/Needle-nose_pliers" title="Needle-nose pliers">needle-nose pliers</a> designed by Fauchard in the late 17th century to use in <a href="/wiki/Prosthodontics" title="Prosthodontics">prosthodontics</a></div></div></div>
<p>The first book focused solely on dentistry was the "Artzney Buchlein" in 1530,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-History_Of_Dentistry_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-History_Of_Dentistry-48">[46]</a></sup> and the first dental textbook written in English was called "Operator for the Teeth" by Charles Allen in 1685.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bdatimeline_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-bdatimeline-24">[23]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the United Kingdom, there was no formal qualification for the providers of dental treatment until 1859 and it was only in 1921 that the practice of dentistry was limited to those who were professionally qualified. The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Commission_on_the_National_Health_Service" title="Royal Commission on the National Health Service">Royal Commission on the National Health Service</a> in 1979 reported that there were then more than twice as many registered dentists per 10,000 population in the UK than there were in 1921.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[56]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_dentistry">Modern dentistry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dentistry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Modern dentistry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Microscope,The_Dental_cosmos_(1907).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1964" data-file-width="1824" decoding="async" height="237" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Microscope%2CThe_Dental_cosmos_%281907%29.jpg/220px-Microscope%2CThe_Dental_cosmos_%281907%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Microscope%2CThe_Dental_cosmos_%281907%29.jpg/330px-Microscope%2CThe_Dental_cosmos_%281907%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Microscope%2CThe_Dental_cosmos_%281907%29.jpg/440px-Microscope%2CThe_Dental_cosmos_%281907%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Microscope,The_Dental_cosmos_(1907).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A microscopic device used in dental analysis, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1907</span></div></div></div>
<p>It was between 1650 and 1800 that the science of modern dentistry developed. The English physician <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Browne" title="Thomas Browne">Thomas Browne</a> in his <i><a href="/wiki/A_Letter_to_a_Friend" title="A Letter to a Friend">A Letter to a Friend</a></i> (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1656</span> pub. 1690) made an early dental observation with characteristic humour:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The Egyptian Mummies that I have seen, have had their Mouths open, and somewhat gaping, which affordeth a good opportunity to view and observe their Teeth, wherein 'tis not easie to find any wanting or decayed: and therefore in Egypt, where one Man practised but one Operation, or the Diseases but of single Parts, it must needs be a barren Profession to confine unto that of drawing of Teeth, and little better than to have been Tooth-drawer unto King Pyrrhus, who had but two in his Head.</p></blockquote>
<p>The French surgeon <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Fauchard" title="Pierre Fauchard">Pierre Fauchard</a> became known as the "father of modern dentistry". Despite the limitations of the primitive surgical instruments during the late 17th and early 18th century, Fauchard was a highly skilled <a href="/wiki/Surgeon" title="Surgeon">surgeon</a> who made remarkable improvisations of dental instruments, often adapting tools from <a href="/wiki/Watchmaker" title="Watchmaker">watchmakers</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jeweler" title="Jeweler">jewelers</a> and even <a href="/wiki/Barber" title="Barber">barbers</a>, that he thought could be used in dentistry. He introduced <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dental_filling" title="Dental filling">dental fillings</a> as treatment for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dental_cavities" title="Dental cavities">dental cavities</a>. He asserted that <a href="/wiki/Sugar" title="Sugar">sugar</a>-derived acids like <a href="/wiki/Tartaric_acid" title="Tartaric acid">tartaric acid</a> were responsible for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caries" title="Caries">dental decay</a>, and also suggested that tumors surrounding the teeth and in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gingiva" title="Gingiva">gums</a> could appear in the later stages of tooth decay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Besombes_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Besombes-59">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weinberger_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Weinberger-60">[58]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Panoramic_radiograph_of_historic_dental_implants.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="904" data-file-width="1350" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Panoramic_radiograph_of_historic_dental_implants.jpg/220px-Panoramic_radiograph_of_historic_dental_implants.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Panoramic_radiograph_of_historic_dental_implants.jpg/330px-Panoramic_radiograph_of_historic_dental_implants.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Panoramic_radiograph_of_historic_dental_implants.jpg/440px-Panoramic_radiograph_of_historic_dental_implants.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Panoramic_radiograph_of_historic_dental_implants.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Panoramic radiograph of historic dental implants, made 1978</div></div></div>
<p>Fauchard was the pioneer of <a href="/wiki/Prosthodontics" title="Prosthodontics">dental prosthesis</a>, and he invented many methods to replace lost teeth. He suggested that substitutes could be made from carved blocks of <a href="/wiki/Ivory" title="Ivory">ivory</a> or <a href="/wiki/Bone" title="Bone">bone</a>. He also introduced <a href="/wiki/Dental_braces" title="Dental braces">dental braces</a>, although they were initially made of gold, he discovered that the teeth position could be corrected as the teeth would follow the pattern of the wires. Waxed <a href="/wiki/Linen" title="Linen">linen</a> or <a href="/wiki/Silk" title="Silk">silk</a> threads were usually employed to fasten the braces. His contributions to the world of dental science consist primarily of his 1728 publication Le chirurgien dentiste or The Surgeon Dentist.  The French text included "basic oral anatomy and function, dental construction, and various operative and restorative techniques, and effectively separated dentistry from the wider category of surgery".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Besombes_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-Besombes-59">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weinberger_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-Weinberger-60">[58]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dental_office.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1134" data-file-width="1512" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Dental_office.jpg/220px-Dental_office.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Dental_office.jpg/330px-Dental_office.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Dental_office.jpg/440px-Dental_office.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dental_office.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A modern dentist's chair</div></div></div>
<p>After Fauchard, the study of dentistry rapidly expanded. Two important books, <i>Natural History of Human Teeth</i> (1771) and <i>Practical Treatise on the Diseases of the Teeth</i> (1778), were published by British surgeon <a href="/wiki/John_Hunter_(surgeon)" title="John Hunter (surgeon)">John Hunter</a>. In 1763 he entered into a period of collaboration with the London-based dentist James Spence. He began to theorise about the possibility of <a href="/wiki/Tooth_transplant" title="Tooth transplant">tooth transplants</a> from one person to another. He realised that the chances of a successful tooth transplant (initially, at least) would be improved if the donor tooth was as fresh as possible and was matched for size with the recipient.  These principles are still used in the transplantation of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Internal_organ" title="Internal organ">internal organs</a>. Hunter conducted a series of pioneering operations, in which he attempted a tooth transplant. Although the donated teeth never properly bonded with the recipients' gums, one of Hunter's patients stated that he had three which lasted for six years, a remarkable achievement for the period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[59]</a></sup>
</p><p>Major advances in science were made in the 19th century, and dentistry evolved from a trade to a profession. The profession came under government regulation by the end of the 19th century. In the UK the Dentist Act was passed in 1878 and the British Dental Association formed in 1879. In the same year, <a href="/wiki/Francis_Brodie_Imlach" title="Francis Brodie Imlach">Francis Brodie Imlach</a> was the first ever dentist to be elected President of the Royal College of Surgeons (Edinburgh), raising dentistry onto a par with clinical surgery for the first time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[60]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hazards_in_modern_dentistry">Hazards in modern dentistry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dentistry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Hazards in modern dentistry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Occupational_hazards_in_dentistry" title="Occupational hazards in dentistry">Occupational hazards in dentistry</a></div>
<p>Long term occupational noise exposure can contribute to permanent hearing loss, which is referred to as <a href="/wiki/Noise-induced_hearing_loss" title="Noise-induced hearing loss">noise-induced hearing loss</a> (NIHL) and <a href="/wiki/Tinnitus" title="Tinnitus">tinnitus</a>. Noise exposure can cause excessive stimulation of the hearing mechanism, which damages the delicate structures of the inner ear.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[61]</a></sup> NIHL can occur when an individual is exposed to sound levels above 90 dBA according to the <a href="/wiki/Occupational_Safety_and_Health_Administration" title="Occupational Safety and Health Administration">Occupational Safety and Health Administration</a> (OSHA). Regulations state that the permissible noise exposure levels for individuals is 90 dBA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[62]</a></sup> For the National Institute for Occupational Safety and Health (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NIOSH" title="NIOSH">NIOSH</a>), exposure limits are set to 85 dBA. Exposures below 85 dBA are not considered to be hazardous. Time limits are placed on how long an individual can stay in an environment above 85 dBA before it causes hearing loss. OSHA places that limitation at 8 hours for 85 dBA. The exposure time becomes shorter as the dBA level increases.
</p><p>Within the field of dentistry, a variety of cleaning tools are used including piezoelectric and sonic scalers, and ultrasonic scalers and cleaners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[63]</a></sup> While a majority of the tools do not exceed 75 dBA,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[64]</a></sup> prolonged exposure over many years can lead to hearing loss or complaints of tinnitus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[65]</a></sup> Few dentists have reported using personal hearing protective devices,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[67]</a></sup> which could offset any potential hearing loss or tinnitus.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Evidence-based_dentistry">Evidence-based dentistry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dentistry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Evidence-based dentistry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Evidence-based_dentistry" title="Evidence-based dentistry">Evidence-based dentistry</a></div>
<p>There is a movement in modern dentistry to place a greater emphasis on high-quality scientific evidence in decision-making. <a href="/wiki/Evidence-based_dentistry" title="Evidence-based dentistry">Evidence-based dentistry</a> (EBD) uses current scientific evidence to guide decisions. It is an approach to oral health that requires the application and examination of relevant scientific data related to the patient's oral and medical health. Along with the dentist's professional skill and expertise, EBD allows dentists to stay up to date on the latest procedures and patients to receive improved treatment. A new paradigm for medical education designed to incorporate current research into education and practice was developed to help practitioners provide the best care for their patients.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[68]</a></sup> It was first introduced by <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Guyatt" title="Gordon Guyatt">Gordon Guyatt</a> and the Evidence-Based Medicine Working Group at <a href="/wiki/McMaster_University" title="McMaster University">McMaster University</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ontario,_Canada" title="Ontario, Canada">Ontario, Canada</a> in the 1990s. It is part of the larger movement toward <a href="/wiki/Evidence-based_medicine" title="Evidence-based medicine">evidence-based medicine</a> and other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evidence-based_practices" title="Evidence-based practices">evidence-based practices</a>, especially since a major part of dentistry involves dealing with oral and systemic diseases. Other issues relevant to the dental field in terms of evidence-based research and evidence-based practice include population oral health, dental clinical practice, tooth morphology etc. 
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dental_Chair_UMSOD.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Dental_Chair_UMSOD.jpg/220px-Dental_Chair_UMSOD.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Dental_Chair_UMSOD.jpg/330px-Dental_Chair_UMSOD.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Dental_Chair_UMSOD.jpg/440px-Dental_Chair_UMSOD.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dental_Chair_UMSOD.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Dental Chair at the University of Michigan School of Dentistry</div></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethical_and_medicolegal_issues">Ethical and medicolegal issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dentistry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Ethical and medicolegal issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Dentistry is unique in that it requires dental students to have competence-based clinical skills that can only be acquired through supervised specialized laboratory training and direct patient care.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[69]</a></sup> This necessitates the need for a scientific and professional basis of care with a foundation of extensive research-based education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[70]</a></sup> According to some experts, the accreditation of dental schools can enhance the quality and professionalism of dental education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[72]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dentistry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Whether Dentists are referred to as "Doctor" is subject to geographic variation. For example, they are called "Doctor" in the US. In the UK, dentists have traditionally been referred to as "Mister" as they identified themselves with <a href="/wiki/Barber_surgeon" title="Barber surgeon">barber surgeons</a> more than <a href="/wiki/Physician" title="Physician">physicians</a> (as do surgeons in the UK, see <a href="/wiki/Surgeon#Titles" title="Surgeon">Surgeon#Titles</a>). However more UK dentists now refer to themselves as "Doctor", although this was considered to be potentially misleading by the British public in a single report  (see Costley and Fawcett 2010).</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-30"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-30">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The scope of Oral and maxillofacial surgery is variable. In some countries, both a medical and dental degree is required for training, and the scope includes head and neck oncology and craniofacial deformity.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
